<span id="freeTextContainer9449716663553114214"><b>3.5 Sweetness Stars</b><br/><br/><b>This book was adorably awkward, funny and cute as fuck!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448323873ra/17122497.gif' width='400' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The MC, Bliss (which some Deity somewhere help me, can these NA names get any more special snowflake?!) is a virgin. Which is generally a big no-no for me, but in this case I actually liked it. She decides, with the help of her <i>loving</i> friend, that she just needs to get rid of that sweater already...<br/><br/>And she is COMPLETELY insane and awkward. And it’s amazing!!!<br/><br/><i> “Stop! Cats! Stop!”</i><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439563897ra/15853829.gif' width='497' height='304' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>In the contrived way that IS the romance g</span>
  <span id="freeText9449716663553114214" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Sweetness Stars</b><br><br><b>This book was adorably awkward, funny and cute as fuck!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448323873ra/17122497.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The MC, Bliss (which some Deity somewhere help me, can these NA names get any more special snowflake?!) is a virgin. Which is generally a big no-no for me, but in this case I actually liked it. She decides, with the help of her <i>loving</i> friend, that she just needs to get rid of that sweater already...<br><br>And she is COMPLETELY insane and awkward. And it’s amazing!!!<br><br><i> “Stop! Cats! Stop!”</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439563897ra/15853829.gif" width="497" height="304" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>In the contrived way that IS the romance genre, the guy who she almost losses it to and her are thrust together by life and circumstance – <b>on several occasions. </b> And it’s a touch overly dramatic what with the whole teacher/student trope (that is REALLY minor here, so if you hate that trope understand that there are MAYBE five years age difference here and he is her university ACTING teacher not, like, her Math 12 teacher or something like that which would make me puke all over the place.)<br><br>The part about this book that I enjoyed the most was the general sweetness of these two together. Yes Bliss is awkward – a la Zooey Deschanel (or preferable Rory &amp; Dean days Rory) but it’s hilarious and cute and completely how I imagine I would have been had my life taken a different road. Carmack magnifies the little moments so well! The handholding, the innocent touch of hand on flesh, the kissing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436207028ra/15431887.gif" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I did roll my eyes a few times while reading this story but far more often I laughed or made that d’aww noise in the back of my throat. What I have to applaud Carmack for is bringing the sensual aspect into this novel, rather than the far more common sexual vein. <br><br>Recommended to those craving a sweet fix with a side of British accent!<br><br><b>Category: A Book by an Author I’ve Never Read Before.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/stories/1431553936p8/397547.jpg" width="420" height="290.4" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_419934009" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419934009" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3060045-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350249427p2/3060045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419934009?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3060045-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419934009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7148561024791677614">Another reread, and I STILL LOVE IT!!! *sigh*<br/><br/>*******************************<br/><br/>Full review to come on Reading Lark (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readinglark.blogspot.com'>www.readinglark.blogspot.com</a>) on October 21st. Suffice it to say that:<br/><br/>1) I SERIOUSLY LOVED THIS BOOK<br/><br/>2) It made me have feelings of the goosebumps & butterflies in stomach variety.<br/><br/>3) I am immediately rereading this. <br/><br/>UH-MAZE-ING!<br/><br/><b>*full review follows this* </b><br/><br/>This is only the second time I have ever immediately reread a book upon finishing it - the other time was when I read the Twilight sa</span>
  <span id="freeText7148561024791677614" style="display:none">Another reread, and I STILL LOVE IT!!! *sigh*<br /><br />*******************************<br /><br />Full review to come on Reading Lark (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readinglark.blogspot.com">www.readinglark.blogspot.com</a>) on October 21st. Suffice it to say that:<br /><br />1) I SERIOUSLY LOVED THIS BOOK<br /><br />2) It made me have feelings of the goosebumps &amp; butterflies in stomach variety.<br /><br />3) I am immediately rereading this. <br /><br />UH-MAZE-ING!<br /><br /><b>*full review follows this* </b><br /><br />This is only the second time I have ever immediately reread a book upon finishing it - the other time was when I read the Twilight saga. What will follow may contain serious gushing about how much I loved this book, but I'm going to lead out with a warning: I don't for a minute imagine that everyone will feel like I did about this book. Losing It seems to have caught me at the right time in my life, in the right mood, and it totally swept me away. <br /><br />Losing It is the story of Bliss; a heroine who I just adore. She's a late developer and makes things hard on herself, which is why she's at the end of her college years and still a virgin. She's pretty, intelligent, funny, and she doesn't really believe that she is. She is kind of desperate to lose her virginity, but at the same time she is totally freaked out by the idea. One night her BFF talks her into getting it over with, and with some liquid courage she finds herself talking to a hot stranger in a bar. This is the point at which I could have rolled my eyes and wandered off to make a cup of tea - if not for the writing. I loved the word play, the zinging back and forth and Bliss's inner dialogue which was almost exactly what I would have been thinking... a lovely mix of disbelief, glee, and sarcasm. <br /><br />My fangirl love was sealed when, following a ridiculously hot scene, Bliss freaked out, yelled something about a fictitious pet cat, and ran out of her own flat into the middle of the night in her undies. How could I not love such a lunatic?! Better yet that she recognized her own insanity and then berated herself. I think there's not a woman alive that couldn't relate to that, at least in part. I was sucked in by the romance but I stayed because Bliss totally won me over - she actually went out and rescued a cat to try and cover up her insanity! I seriously love that character! (I am also a sucker for a well written cat, and Hamlet was fabulous!) <br /><br />As for the lover boy... Garrick was such a swoonsome hero that it wasn't hard to lust after him like Bliss did. I usually get really irritated when people try to write British men in books, because the Hugh Grant stereotype hasn't ever done a thing for me, but happily although Garrick was British he wasn't a Hugh clone. He was just the right mix of sexy grinning and dashing gentleman, sprinkled with a smidgen of sexual predator that made both Bliss and I go weak at the knees. I also really enjoyed the forbidden nature of Bliss and Garrick's relationship. I first enjoyed the student/teacher angle in the Vampire Academy series by Richelle Mead, followed it up with Half Blood by Jennifer Armentrout, and I think Losing It this is another great example, although I would say Losing It is definitely for older readers than those other stories. <br /><br />This was a hot HOT story. I won't lie - I wouldn't give this to any teenager. I would absolutely hand this out to young women in their 20s and give them a wink though! I am eager to explore other reads coming out in the New Adult genre after this book - the sexuality of the book was just the right side of the adult romance genre and just the wrong side of YA fiction to feel utterly pitch perfect to me. It left me seriously hot under the collar, covered in goosebumps and wishing I wasn't quite so single. There is a marvelous build up of sexual tension through the book to the inevitable departure of Bliss's virginity, and I wouldn't have changed a single word. It was fun, seductive and full of just the right amount of red faced humiliation to suck me in and keep me glued to my Kindle until I had finished the book... twice. <br /><br />Full marks to the Cara Cormack - she's on my 'to watch' list, and I will be watching and waiting to get a copy of this in hard back for my super special shelf in the bookcase. <br /><br /><br /><br />RELEASE DATES:<br /><br />USA paperback 2/26/13<br />UK and Australia paperback: 3/28/13</span>
  <a data-text-id="7148561024791677614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20266662-carvanz?shelf=virgin-h">virgin-h</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939680160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11406656468374600423">This is a light, fluffy, fun read. I really enjoyed the author’s “voice” but the pacing the first half of the book seemed slow due to the fact that Bliss and Garrick don’t have a lot of in-depth interactions. However, during that time there is plenty of knowledge shared about what takes place at a school for theater arts. Unfortunately I’m not a big theater fan. I know, go ahead, skin me but it’s true. I’m a central Texas girl living in the country so it’s not something I’ve ever been exposed to</span>
  <span id="freeText11406656468374600423" style="display:none">This is a light, fluffy, fun read. I really enjoyed the author’s “voice” but the pacing the first half of the book seemed slow due to the fact that Bliss and Garrick don’t have a lot of in-depth interactions. However, during that time there is plenty of knowledge shared about what takes place at a school for theater arts. Unfortunately I’m not a big theater fan. I know, go ahead, skin me but it’s true. I’m a central Texas girl living in the country so it’s not something I’ve ever been exposed to. Despite that, I laughed out loud so many times with Bliss and her friends. She has some amazing friends and I’m pretty sure they’re going to get their books as well. <br /><br />Once I felt the connection with Bliss and Garrick I was able to settle down and truly enjoy the story. This is a very low angst book written in the heroine’s POV with some push and pull. The epilogue was sweet and written totally from Garrick’s view point. I wish this author had given me more of his inner musings because instead of just liking this book I would have loved this book. There is no other woman drama, the hero is no manwhore, and there is no abuse or violence. <br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer422855297" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17165033981258527289">I'm happy to say that this is one of the rare books that I think is better on audio than it would have been reading it. Which was lovely, because for the longest time, the cover made me cringe, and kept me from giving it a shot. Who wants their visuals of the sexy teacher in a teacher/student romance to look like a pale, scrawny fourteen year old? Not me. Interestingly enough, this must not have been my sentiment alone because there are two cover versions. <br/><br/>This:<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16034964.Losing_It__Losing_It___1_' title='Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1348459319s/16034964.jpg' alt='Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>and this:<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17375832.Losing_It__Losing_It___1_' title='Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1361317540s/17375832.jpg' alt='Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Much improved!!<br/><br/>Ok</span>
  <span id="freeText17165033981258527289" style="display:none">I'm happy to say that this is one of the rare books that I think is better on audio than it would have been reading it. Which was lovely, because for the longest time, the cover made me cringe, and kept me from giving it a shot. Who wants their visuals of the sexy teacher in a teacher/student romance to look like a pale, scrawny fourteen year old? Not me. Interestingly enough, this must not have been my sentiment alone because there are two cover versions. <br><br>This:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16034964.Losing_It__Losing_It___1_" title="Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1348459319s/16034964.jpg" alt="Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>and this:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17375832.Losing_It__Losing_It___1_" title="Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1361317540s/17375832.jpg" alt="Losing It (Losing It, #1) by Cora Carmack" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Much improved!!<br><br>Okay, moving on. (I feel so shallow, but cover love, I had not.)<br><br>Quick recap of the story: Bliss is a twenty-something senior theater major in college and somehow still holding on to her V-card. Every parent's dream, eh? But she's determined to finally lose the pesky thing and with the help of her best friend, goes trolling in the bar one night. With a little more help in the form of liquid courage, she meets a man...reading a book in the bar, who opens his sexy mouth and out comes a British accent along with a smile and definite interest in his eyes. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395973086i/9070666.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><blockquote></blockquote>I was going to have sex.<br>With a boy.<br>A hot boy.<br>A hot BRITISH boy.<br>Or maybe I was going to throw up.<br>What if I threw up on the hot British boy?<br>What if I threw up on the hot British boy DURING SEX?”</b><br><br>One thing leads to another, and the next morning, she walks into class and guess who teach is? Yep, the dude from last night. <br><br>So I enjoyed this story so much more than I thought I would. There are some really iffy reviews out there but I connected with both Bliss and Garrick. Both are really great people. No one does anything totally stupid, Bliss doesn't act like a complete pushover. In fact, this was quite the easy book to sink into. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395973086i/9070667._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I enjoyed the theater angle of the story. You could tell that the author feels a passion for it. It was interesting to get a different perspective on it, to get some insight on how hard it must be for people who love the stage to choose that as a career, knowing that the likelihood of making a living in the performing arts is not the most reliable choice...that they may have to settle for production or stage management and watch someone else live out their dreams.<br><br>Bliss' inner dialogue was hilarious at times. She's not the most confident of people but she doesn't come across as a complete tool either. She's a bit shy, not quite sure of herself but not a doormat either. I love how she tended to just blurt out the most random things when she was nervous or backed into a corner. One such word explosion of which ended up in Bliss owning a cat named Hamlet that really hated her.<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395973086i/9070668.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She has a really great group of friends, which brings me to my one point of contention with the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really hated that her best friend, the guy one, ends up crushing on her and then being all upset when she wants to keep it just friends.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's not so much that I hated it as a plot device, but it was just so awkward, and was the biggest wrench in the story...even more so than the teacher thing. That relationship always felt inevitable to me. <br><br>Predictable? Yes, but the story was lovely anyways. <br><br>Will I continue the series? Definitely. <br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17165033981258527289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WpnkJAhqqZppENkXEDALRePy+yGX6f6jKvV71VvjgDhgv432szRg8s47bXbnxQGaNa0c6VlkcMRxiz1klqByog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

  <span id="freeText2748712288593327803" style="display:none">Cora Carmack is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of New Adult Romance and YA fantasy. Her books have been translated into more than a dozen languages around the world. Cora lives in Austin, TX, and on any given day you might find her typing away at her computer, flying to various cities around the world, or just watching Netflix with her kitty Katniss and her dog Sherlock. But she can always be found on Twitter, Facebook, Instagram, Pinterest, and her website <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.coracarmack.com">www.coracarmack.com</a>.<br /><br />***Please note: I am rarely on goodreads, so if you're trying to get a hold of me, the best places to find me are Twitter, Facebook, my blog, Instagram, and via email (coracarmack(at)gmail(dot)com). </span>
